## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws in solid mechanics/materials science (elasticity, plasticity, and thermoelastic/thermal-softening behavior). Likely relationships include an elastic stress–strain law with temperature-dependent modulus and/or temperature-dependent yield/flow stress with strain hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic Hooke law (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic response with E(T) ≈ linear in T)
- Exponential modulus softening (polymer/metal softening proxy): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (E(T) varying roughly exponentially over a range)
- Polynomial nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (weakly nonlinear elastic response, temperature-dependent stiffness)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type, temperature-modulated): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (plastic-like hardening in monotonic loading with temperature effect lumped into prefactor)
- Voce-type saturating hardening in strain (temperature-dependent scale): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (c2 + (1 - c2) * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon))) (hardening that approaches a saturation level; T affects overall level)
- Ramberg–Osgood-inspired explicit form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (1 + c2 * epsilon**c3) (captures initial linearity and reduced tangent modulus at larger strain)
- Thermal-softening multiplicative factor (Johnson–Cook-like, no strain-rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (strain hardening times a temperature softening/amplification factor; sign of c3 sets softening vs stiffening)
- Bilinear elastoplastic surrogate (smooth yield transition): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon - (c2 + c3 * T) * log(1 + exp(c4 * (epsilon - (c5 + c6 * T)))) (elastic regime transitioning to reduced slope/hardening after yield strain that shifts with T)
- Thermal strain offset (effective strain): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - (c2 + c3 * T)) (thermoelastic stress from mechanical strain minus thermal/eigenstrain approximation)
- Buckling/instability-like softening proxy (stress peaks then drops): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (rises at small strain, decays beyond a peak; T scales peak level)
- Piecewise-like tension/compression asymmetry surrogate (if epsilon spans sign): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * Abs(epsilon) (different slopes in tension vs compression via Abs term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic modulus changing with temperature → multiply epsilon by a T-dependent prefactor such as (c0 + c1*T) or c0*exp(c1*T).
- Thermal expansion/eigenstrain effects → use an effective strain shift (epsilon - g(T)), producing nonzero stress at epsilon = 0 when constrained.
- Strain hardening in plasticity → power laws in epsilon (epsilon**c) or saturating exponentials (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) added/multiplied to a base stress level.
- Smooth elastic-to-plastic transition (no explicit piecewise allowed) → use softplus/log(1+exp(·)) or tanh-like transitions centered at a yield strain that can depend on T.
- Thermal softening of flow stress → multiply the strain-dependent part by an exponential-in-T or a decreasing rational-in-T factor (e.g., exp(c*T) with c<0), indicating reduced stress at higher T.
- Nonlinear elasticity at moderate strains → include odd powers of epsilon (epsilon**3, epsilon**5) possibly with T-dependent coefficients to reflect anharmonicity and temperature sensitivity.
- Peak-and-drop behavior (damage/necking/instability proxy) without extra state variables → epsilon * exp(-c*epsilon) or similar peaked forms, with T scaling the peak height/location.
- T-dependent yield point shift → let the transition location be (c0 + c1*T) inside a smooth step/softplus argument, representing lower yield strain/stress at elevated temperatures.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
```

With c2 = c6 = 330.2004199209183, let me denote this common value as K.

Expanding:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*K + c3) + c5*epsilon^c4*(T - K)
```

This gives:
```
-c0*c1*epsilon*T + c0*(c1*K + c3)*epsilon + c5*epsilon^c4*T - c5*K*epsilon^c4
```

So the GT has the form:
```
A*epsilon*T + B*epsilon + C*epsilon^c4*T + D*epsilon^c4
```

Where:
- A = -c0*c1 = -23.788 * 0.05042 ≈ -1.1994
- B = c0*(c1*K + c3) = 23.788*(0.05042*330.2 + 1) = 23.788*(16.645 + 1) = 23.788*17.645 ≈ 419.74
- C = c5 = 5.2295
- D = -c5*K = -5.2295*330.2 ≈ -1726.8
- c4 = 0.9585

So GT = A*T*epsilon + B*epsilon + C*T*epsilon^0.9585 + D*epsilon^0.9585

The basis functions are: {T*epsilon, epsilon, T*epsilon^c4, epsilon^c4} where c4 ≈ 0.9585.

Since epsilon ≥ 0 (domain constraint), |epsilon| = epsilon, and epsilon^c4 is well-defined.

Now let me check each candidate. For a match, the candidate must be expressible with exactly these four basis functions (or equivalent).

### Candidate 1:
`T*c0*|ε| + T*c1*|ε|^c2 + c3*|ε| + c4*|ε|^2 + c5*|ε|^c2`

With |ε| = ε: T*ε + T*ε^c2 + ε + ε^2 + ε^c2

Has ε^2 term which GT doesn't have. Can we set c4=0? Yes! Then: T*c0*ε + T*c1*ε^c2 + c3*ε + c5*ε^c2. This matches the GT structure with c2 = 0.9585.

Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 2:
`T*c0*ε + T*c1*|ε|^c2 + c3*|ε|^2 + c4*ε + c5*|ε|^c2`

Set c3=0: T*c0*ε + T*c1*ε^c2 + c4*ε + c5*ε^c2. This matches GT structure.

Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 3:

Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 4:
